<div id="review_359196540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/359196540" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/359196540?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359196540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9602459537428383369">Can someone please come and erase my memory such that I can fall in love again with this story in 2014?<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/review-pivot-point.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382514i/740404.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I really have a hard time believing that I will be able to sit still and wait a whole year for my favorite part of this story. I am even scared. I saw Addie fall in love 2 times (and I loved both love stories – well, one more than the other) and now I expect the next ‘beginning’ to be just as sweet.<br/>I know, this is not the way to start my review, but how do you expect me to focus on writing </span>
  <span id="freeText9602459537428383369" style="display:none">Can someone please come and erase my memory such that I can fall in love again with this story in 2014?<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/review-pivot-point.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382514i/740404.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I really have a hard time believing that I will be able to sit still and wait a whole year for my favorite part of this story. I am even scared. I saw Addie fall in love 2 times (and I loved both love stories – well, one more than the other) and now I expect the next ‘beginning’ to be just as sweet.<br>I know, this is not the way to start my review, but how do you expect me to focus on writing when the ending hit me with the force of a hurricane?<br><br>I LOVE(D) this story.<br>I loved Addie, I loved her friendship with Laila, I loved both love-stories, I loved how fun the writing was and how emotionally invested I got (without even noticing until I fell deeply in love with this book).<br><br>COVER:<br><br>It is so beautiful and I love how it shows the reflected futures, even though I wish the girl had curly hair in one side and a stripe of blue in the other.<br><br>CONCEPT:<br><br>A tiny world inside our world, with supernatural people and their supernatural powers and advanced technologies? A girl that needs to choose a path and that can see both futures in the need to figure out her choice? An unusual love triangle, that it is not even that but two swoon-worthy love stories, that could pin you in place reading and reading and doing nothing more than reading? I’ve been having a hard time finding a book to read in the past few weeks, but this beauty here reminds me of why I love reading so damn much!<br><br><blockquote>“One person can’t change the future. Do you know how many people and things are involved in every major event that happens? Sure, you might be able to change some of the minor aspects of a day, but ultimately things that are going to happen, if you go along a certain path, do happen.”</blockquote><br><br>MAIN CHARACTER:<br><br>Addie is great. She is strong, she is smart, she is cute.. She is a great friend and even with her flaws she is a great person. She cares about her loved ones, she cares about doing things right, she would do whatever it takes to keep things in place even when it can cost her her own heart and happiness (and safety).<br><br>Addie has to make a big decision and it is not about what parent to choose or what boyfriend, it is about so much more.. I am a bit cryptic, but really I don’t want to spoil anything for you.<br><br>I could understand her insecurities, her need to be ‘someone’, to not be defined by her powers; her need to be loved and to love; her need to save (friendships, her heart, even someone’s life). There were so many things happening in her life, it is hard for me to pick one that defined her. I usually get annoyed by the main character and their choices, but this was so not the case. Even when my heart was screaming for her not to do a particular thing, my mind (the traitor!) understood her, approved of her actions.<br><br><blockquote>“It was hard when I knew I was about to be flooded with memories of a life I hadn’t lived yet. Really, two lives I hadn’t lived yet.”</blockquote><br><br>FRIENDSHIP:<br><br>Laila was the best and the funnies friend ever.<br>I loved their little chats, their encouragements, their teasing, the way they tried to help each other. I almost got my heart broken at some point, but I was glad to quickly gather the missing pieces and put them back together.<br>Also I loved their friends, their interaction, the way their stories overlapped in the 2 version of the future. I loved to see that Addie and Laila made similar decisions when not influenced by the others. What can I say, it was all such a fun ride!<br><br>LOVE:<br>This is what I would have loved to read for Valentine’s. There are 2 different love stories and up until some point they were both so sweet and cute and giggle-inducing that I should be ashamed for loving them so much.<br><br>First we have Duke – the beginning of their relationship was the best. I laughed so much because he was so funny and together they were the cutest couple (Note to self: I loved it when he brought that movie to her house). Even though they had almost nothing in common and Addie usually didn’t like “obvious” boys, they did get along very well and made me laugh more than not.<br><br>Then we have Trevor – their story started slower and it was a lot more complicated. He was not the golden boy, but (and maybe even because of that) if I could pick one guy for some reason it would always be him.. (Note to self: I loved the zombie notes). They started as friends and developed into so much more. And I don’t want to influence you in any way, so I’ll keep quiet now.<br><br>Or not so quiet after all.<br>I won’t tell you what choice did Addie make, but looking back I think it was the right one. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Do you hear my heart crying? It was the right choice but it still broke my heart to pieces. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I can’t wait to see how all this will play out in the next book and I hate book series because my patience is running low and also because I am afraid that maybe I won’t love the next book just as much. And this one was perfect.<br>I got to fall in love twice in the same story, and there was no cliché love triangle, and you know how much I enjoy seeing people fall in love – it’s my favorite part of every story (and the thought that I might get my 3rd love story in the next book makes me so excited that I might develop a superpower myself: noting special, just that my excitement might become a bit too contagious).<br><br>CONCLUSIONS:<br><br>So I was wrong, I didn’t know who the Mood Controller really was, but I was close enough because I knew who the bad guy was (and those 2 things are closely related). I still wonder about some things – like how could someone fake a super-power and also the secondary plot about the football players was never fully revealed and explained, but we will have enough time in the next installment for that.<br><br>All I an left to say is that this book has really made my day.<br>Yes, in fact I had a horrible day and it cheered me up in a heartbeat – it made me smile, it made me dream, it made me giggle like a kid, it made me swoon, it made me hope.. and also it made me hate the brief ending because I wanted so much more. 2014, please come faster!<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/review-pivot-point.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696540.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> * This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/review-pivot-point.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_400911701" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400911701" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400911701?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400911701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13527732215751857202"><b>Pivot Point</b> was a wonderfully fast paced and exciting read. I was mesmerized from the first page. While it didn’t’ leave off on a cliffhanger, it’s going to be torture waiting for the next installment!<br/><br/>Addison is a girl with special powers living in a city held secret from the outside world; a city where other “paranormals” live and perfect their abilities. Addison has the ability to search her future and see the outcome of a path she takes. She doesn’t use her ability all the time, so when her p</span>
  <span id="freeText13527732215751857202" style="display:none"><b>Pivot Point</b> was a wonderfully fast paced and exciting read. I was mesmerized from the first page. While it didn’t’ leave off on a cliffhanger, it’s going to be torture waiting for the next installment!<br /><br />Addison is a girl with special powers living in a city held secret from the outside world; a city where other “paranormals” live and perfect their abilities. Addison has the ability to search her future and see the outcome of a path she takes. She doesn’t use her ability all the time, so when her parents announce they’re getting a divorce, she has quite a shock. Addie is now faced with two choices: stay with her mom inside the Compound or go live with her dad in the outside with the “Norms.” Being this is such a huge decision, she performs a search to see what decision to make. Laid out before her are two very different possible futures. If she stays with her mother, she stays with what she knows and has the opportunity to expand and perfect her powers. Addie also sees the star quarterback of her school, Duke, in that future. If Addie goes with her father, she gets to experience life on the outside, without all the facades and illusions, but life in the real. This is a future where she meets, and becomes close to Trevor, the introspective and sweet “Norm” boy. Both were <i>potentially</i> swoon worthy romances! Here’s a tempting sample (I’ll keep it anonymous): <br /><br /><b>
  <i>His lips tickle my neck as they move along it. Is he trying to drive me crazy?.....His lips come to rest against the soft spot below my ear. I can no longer think straight. It’s then I realize I have a fistful of the back of his shirt. I clutch it tighter. He must consider this encouragement because he takes my face in his hands and presses his lips to mine.* </i>
</b><br /><br />*sigh*<br /><br />I find time travel or time altering themes are often difficult to follow and wrap your brain around. Kasie West did an excellent job keeping it simple and refrained from bogging down the plot with unnecessary details. Yet, I think she gave me enough to make the story interesting, and hold my attention. <br /><br />Each reality is played out in alternating chapters, and I soon found a reality and romance I was partial to. No, I’m not going to tell you which. ;) I found myself becoming impatient for the reality I was rooting for when the story would switch to the other reality. Although, those chapters shed light on the story and gave information I wouldn’t have had otherwise, so they were interesting, too. I must add that there’s some danger and mystery that add to the overall thrill in Pivot Point, and I thought it rounded out the story nicely. <br /><br />This was an impressive debut from Kasie West, and now I can’t wait to get me hands on the next one! It better turn out the way I want it!! <br /><br />*Quote taken from an uncorrected proof and may change in the final copy. <br /><br /><i>A copy was provided by HarperTeen through Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</i><br /><br />You can read this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-pivot-point-by-kasie-west.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13527732215751857202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_536429976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/536429976" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/536429976?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer536429976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9129194527738834918">I sense a disturbing new trend in young adult books of borrowing high concept ideas from other genres, slapping it over your typical relationship drama like a crude veneer, and passing it off as the innovative new thing - and I don't like it. Case in point, <i>Pivot Point</i>, which takes the common enough science fiction idea of alternate futures serving as sort of a life lesson or teaching moment and turns it on its head with all angst, all the time. Believe me, I totally get the appeal of an ability</span>
  <span id="freeText9129194527738834918" style="display:none">I sense a disturbing new trend in young adult books of borrowing high concept ideas from other genres, slapping it over your typical relationship drama like a crude veneer, and passing it off as the innovative new thing - and I don't like it. Case in point, <i>Pivot Point</i>, which takes the common enough science fiction idea of alternate futures serving as sort of a life lesson or teaching moment and turns it on its head with all angst, all the time. Believe me, I totally get the appeal of an ability that lets a person see the consequences of a life changing decision before making it, and if this book was actually about two possible futures stemming from one crucial choice, it would've garnered a much higher rating from me. Instead, what I feel I got is the equivalent of seeing the consequences of ordering onion rings instead of fries for lunch - well, not exactly, but close enough - because nothing really important happens to differentiate the two possible futures until the end, and even then the choice is far more angst driven than life shattering, so I was just bored the whole time because I guess I for one just don't see the appeal of second guessing everything, not when there's really no life lesson involved.<br /><br />Even the reason why Addie, the super special narrator who has the ability to see the consequences of her decisions, needs to make this choice is set up really lamely and feels almost trite. I was rolling my eyes as Mom and Dad sit together on the couch and break the news of their divorce to her, she thinks about it for awhile, then uses her special ability to see which future she prefers - umm, what is this? Do people with powers not suffer from the emotional fallout of parents divorcing like the rest of us normal human beings? Does anyone respond to a line like 'sorry honey but your dad and I haven't had a working relationship in years even though you've never noticed but we're telling you now and by the way we're divorcing' with 'oh ok how strange but now let me think about which one of you I want to live with' - really? I don’t know, but the first half of the book just feels artificial and disconnected from reality, and the entire time I’m left wishing Addie had a sibling or somebody who could've put the divorce in perspective and kept the story emotionally grounded. Of course, that didn't happen, so I ended up having to trudge through alternating chapters between one of Addie's possible futures with her father and another with her mother and needless to say, there's really just no plot to speak of because until almost the very end there really is not much difference between these two alternate realities and the emotions coming off of Addie and her parents don't feel realistic at all. Do I care that in one reality she ends up with fellow superhuman Duke and in the other reality she has a thing for normal person Trevor? Why should I when the only consequences of this 'monumental' choice until the twist ending is having to make new friends versus keeping the same old ones and needing to talk to the best friend by phone instead of in person?<br /><br />Besides the dull, weird, and absent parents and the illusion of choice when there’s no meaningful difference between the two realities besides one twist ending, the writing didn’t work for me either. Because what I said about the high concept being used as a crude veneer is absolutely true - just look at Addie’s descriptions of Duke and her ‘I secretly like him but I know he’s a player and just using me but whatever’ attitude - *head desk*. Ok, I know I’m supposed to give Addie a pass because of what’s revealed about Duke and his abilities, but from how their relationship is written (like a bad rom com even if the dialogue actually kind of works), I don’t think I can. Not when she could be so much better than a walking cliche. And not when the relationship pointlessly spans half the book without Addie really figuring out whether there's any consequence to her picking one parent to live with over the other. Where's the consequences of the supposed life altering decision? What's Addie supposed to learn from these two parallel realities? Then, there’s Addie’s best friend Laila who’s a total ingrate and all around terrible friend basically and Trevor, who is at least written realistically (compared to Duke) - and sympathetic and likable to boot - but I don’t know, I guess in order for the ending to work I have to have cared about Addie and Trevor - and I didn’t.<br /><br />Anyway, maybe it would’ve helped had the superhuman aspect not been a complete bore, but that’s another part of the let down for me. Personally, the appeal of people with superpowers is either like <i>X-Men</i> where they serve as an allegory against discrimination, or like <i>Spider-man</i> where we have something as awesome as Stan Lee’s iconic ‘with great power comes great responsibility’ line, but <i>Pivot Point</i> on the other hand is nothing of the sort. The superpowers are used as more of a joke - telekinetic football!! - and while Kasie West tries to use how different Addie and her fellow superhumans are compared to the ‘Norms’ as a major plot point - it’s just so shallow to the point I really didn’t care about Addie as the superhuman trying to adjust in this ‘Norm’ town. Plus, the actual point of the book, certain characters misusing their superpowers, gets buried beneath chapter after chapter of just Addie going about the most ordinary and dull high school stuff that doesn’t really show why one future is preferable to the other, so much so the climax really didn’t fit well with the rest of the book. Yeah, I think it’s clever how certain things revealed in one possible reality sort of parallels other events in the other reality, simply because the really big events have been ongoing since even before Addie uses her ability, but no matter how much West tries to plant hints and clues like the murdered girls leading up to revealing the big villain, I think she tries too hard adding in a random crazy (because turns out the ending is completely tangential to the whole point of the Search) and making Addie seem like she’s making this big sacrifice out of a <i>possible</i> future and it didn’t work for me.<br /><br />I guess I expected something monumental to happen at the end of the book, something that could’ve justified spending so much time on Addie’s daily life in these two different realities. What actually happens though is a disappointing, crazy villain type moment that not only didn’t fit with the rest of the book but I don’t even get the feeling Addie learns anything about using her powers or us ‘Norms’ from the experience. So, sorry <i>Pivot Point</i>, but you completely missed the whole point of the concept. Meh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9129194527738834918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_355158822" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355158822" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355158822?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a story which hasn't been done a thousand times before</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=hybrid-multiple-genre">hybrid-multiple-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355158822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5834516777309412682"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Two Paths - One Choice.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381858i/739306.jpg' alt=' photo d86c5e5c-6476-40c8-8733-1568b7757efa_zps01622687.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>3.5 stars (but the ending was 5 stars, so hurry up book 2!).<br/><br/>Poor Addie. I have a hard time trying to figure out which restaurant to go to or which movie to watch when given a choice. If you told me to pick between two paths which would lead my life in complete opposite directions, yet both paths might come with their own set of problems...forget it. I would probably end up having a nervous breakdown.<br/><br/>3 second basic story concept : Addie's parents are getting a d</span>
  <span id="freeText5834516777309412682" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Two Paths - One Choice.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381858i/739306.jpg" alt=" photo d86c5e5c-6476-40c8-8733-1568b7757efa_zps01622687.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>3.5 stars (but the ending was 5 stars, so hurry up book 2!).<br><br>Poor Addie. I have a hard time trying to figure out which restaurant to go to or which movie to watch when given a choice. If you told me to pick between two paths which would lead my life in complete opposite directions, yet both paths might come with their own set of problems...forget it. I would probably end up having a nervous breakdown.<br><br>3 second basic story concept : Addie's parents are getting a divorce. Addie has powers which allow her to look into her future. Addie decides to investigate two different futures - one with her mom and one with her dad.<br><br>The first 30% of the book had me sort of frustrated. I knew that I was being set up for what was to come but it's slightly annoying to switch back and forth with the story pov's. Something about the flow reminded me of how I felt while reading <i>Will Grayson, Will Grayson</i>. I distinctly remember enjoying one of the Will povs, but the other not as much. Instead of 2 different Wills, we had 2 of the same Addie in a different setting. One side of the Addie story I really liked. The other side floundered. The chapter headings were a fun little touch to distinguish between 2 different stories which took place in the PARA (special powers) community and the NORM (normal) community.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>The PARA side : the 'not as interesting' half of the story</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381858i/739307.jpg" alt=" photo 4d57f5ff-1da1-4ca4-af14-817ed83dc88d_zps744bd5e7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everyone has special powers in this closeted community. Addie's starting something with the local football hero. You would think that the side of the story in which everyone uses special powers would be the best part, but eh. I guess when everyone can do something and it becomes part of everyday life, this turns out to be just as normal as any other story.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>The NORM side : wins the battle of the dueling worlds</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381858i/739308.jpg" alt=" photo 04e48332-dcc9-4050-ac00-e9e76c53c504_zps97c1c355.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Not surprisingly, I have to go with the lovable artistic guy as a love interest. This side of the story was more interesting because this life was new and different to Addie. For her, learning to use appliances and unlock doors the way everyone else has to IS abnormal. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>My overall thoughts :</b>
</blockquote><br>I spent almost two weeks sitting on this book after reading the first 30%. There was nothing that jumped out and grabbed me about what was going on because everything seemed to be focused on everyday life and the two boys who Addie might have to pick between (which was sort of lackluster imo when you could be focusing more on crazy powers), so I decided to come back when I was ready. But when I did come back, I found myself flying through the rest of the book in less than a couple of hours. Once I started to really focus on the stories as the paths started inching closer to the collision of time when it was 'one or the other,' I realized that Addie was going to get hosed, no matter which path she took. Which immediately made the story that much more interesting, once I realized that it would eventually come to down to more than just <i>which boy should I choose</i>?<br><br>The last part of the book surprised me. I had some suspicions about which path she was going to choose, but didn't realize that so much would need to be altered in order for this to happen. There is a HUGE speed bump which is now going to mess with everything that happens from here on out. I think there's real opportunity for book 2 to have some crazy stuff happen. My hope is that there will be a bigger presence of special abilities and powers. We got pretty far into this book before we started to see the ramifications of messing with potential outcomes.<br><br><i>This book provided from the publisher through Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5834516777309412682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2011909578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56485897-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532735871p2/56485897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/56485897-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alyssa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56485897-alyssa?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56485897-alyssa?shelf=3-5-stars">3-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2011909578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer404141242505490029"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“When I read, I feel emotion all on my own. Emotion no living person is making me feel.”</i>
</blockquote> <br/>This is why I read too 😀 PS. I love you, Addie 💙 <br/><br/><b>Spoilers Beyond. Read @ Your Own Risk :D</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <u>Things I Liked:</u>
</blockquote><br/><br/>✔️ Trevor ( and Brody ) is the definition of a good boyfriend in my book. Does anyone know where I can obtain a Trevor? <br/>✔️ The ending, which completely took me by surprise. I'm so dumb and didn't realize the whole book was a freaking search! Sometimes, I'm so stupid when it comes to readin</span>
  <span id="freeText404141242505490029" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“When I read, I feel emotion all on my own. Emotion no living person is making me feel.”</i>
</blockquote> <br />This is why I read too 😀 PS. I love you, Addie 💙 <br /><br /><b>Spoilers Beyond. Read @ Your Own Risk :D</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>Things I Liked:</u>
</blockquote><br /><br />✔️ Trevor ( and Brody ) is the definition of a good boyfriend in my book. Does anyone know where I can obtain a Trevor? <br />✔️ The ending, which completely took me by surprise. I'm so dumb and didn't realize the whole book was a freaking search! Sometimes, I'm so stupid when it comes to reading, I swear. Anyways, the twist that it really was Bobby all along and wasn't even Poison literally made me gasp out loud. And also how Laila died in one future, I thought it was real. Even though sometimes I may not like her, I didn't want her end to be so tragic. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Because an illusion is an illusion. Reality always exists despite the facade.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>Things I Disliked:</u>
</blockquote><br /><br />✖️ Duke is probably the most stupidest and idiotic jerk I've ever met. <br />✖️ Bobby just makes me want to scream and punch someone in the face. <br />✖️ The beginning of the book ( first 150 pages ) were so boring.<br />✖️ Addie's power ( searching the future / clairvoyance ) : honestly, with such an incredible mind power like this, the fact that she can <b>only see two outcomes and can't do anything about it except choose either one</b> is quite pathetic to me. I'd rather be a Mass Manipulator, anything else beside this lame one. <br />✖️ World building: the Compound is pretty cool, but honestly, the world Ms. West has laid out in Pivot Point is quite flat and has no structure. It just felt like any typical world in a YA novel. The author could've done so much better and went beyond what she wrote when it comes to the Compound. Their world has so much potential and she didn't do anything about it. It just felt so <i>simple.</i> Personally, I like when things are complicated, but to a point where the reader can still understand everything being said and not be confused. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>Overall:</u>
</blockquote><br /><br />Really good story with lots of potential, but in the end, the dislikes ultimately won out, thus the reason for my average rating instead of 5 stars. Don't get me wrong, the story kept me intrigued and was seriously good, just that my problems with the plot line overshadowed the good things 😀<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Sometimes perfection reveals the lie, ..., not the truth."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Rating:</b> ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars<br /><b>Lead Male Character:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ ★ / 5 stars (Trevor) ★ ★ / 5 stars (Duke)<br /><b>Lead Female Character:</b> ★ ★ ★ ★ / 5 stars (Addie) ★ ★ ★ and a half / 5 stars (Laila) <br /><b>Plotline:</b> ★ ★ ★ / 5 stars <br /><b>Genre:</b> Young adult, romance, adventure, sc-fi<br /><b>Will I recommend this book to others?:</b> Sure<br /><b>Will I reread this book?:</b> Only for Trevor &lt;3<br /><b>Overall story summed up in one word:</b> Eh</span>

<div id="review_2059780986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2059780986" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2059780986?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15720403-pivot-point">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=trashtastic">trashtastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=challenge-6wks-summer">challenge-6wks-summer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=3stars">3stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2017">read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=scifi-dystopian">scifi-dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2059780986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14283907038379587514">This book had a very similar feel to the Gwyneth Paltrow film <i>Sliding Doors</i> except with a heavy paranormal aspect. Addie is part of a section of society that have exceptional cognitive powers and abilities making them sorta super human. They live separated from the "norms" in a specially designed secret compound. When there is a decision to be made in Addie's life her unique ability means she can search her future to see the possible outcomes of her choices. So when Addie is given the decision t</span>
  <span id="freeText14283907038379587514" style="display:none">This book had a very similar feel to the Gwyneth Paltrow film <i>Sliding Doors</i> except with a heavy paranormal aspect. Addie is part of a section of society that have exceptional cognitive powers and abilities making them sorta super human. They live separated from the "norms" in a specially designed secret compound. When there is a decision to be made in Addie's life her unique ability means she can search her future to see the possible outcomes of her choices. So when Addie is given the decision to leave the compound with her dad or stay behind with her mum Addie "searches" her future to see the possibilities that each choice could have. The book is set up in alternating chapters of each possible outcome i.e. stay or go.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500247953ra/23314249.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall this was pretty ridiculous, at times frustrating, very predictable and ultimately had a disappointingly written ending. It seriously sucked with its execution. Yet I kinda liked it!!! Addie didn't really annoy me as an MC (always a surprising bonus in YA!) and there was a super cute boy to ship her with (hello Trevor!!).<br><br>So I guess what I'm saying is bring on the sequel! (But if this wasn't a library book I'd borrowed I'd probably be more annoyed...)<br><br>Somewhere between <b>two and a half to three stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14283907038379587514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1206297779" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206297779" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206297779?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=dystopia-sci-fi">dystopia-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206297779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3416367051254937740"><i>
  <b>“Sometimes perfection reveals the lie, not the truth.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Addison is a Searcher, she is able to see all the alternate paths when she has to make a decision. Basically, she's able to see, and live through, all the ways a certain choice will change her future and where that decison would lead. <br/>This story is set in a modern day world, where a secret society of Paranormals with special mind abilities lives in a technologically advanced Compound, only rarely mixing with the Norms - the ordinary peopl</span>
  <span id="freeText3416367051254937740" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Sometimes perfection reveals the lie, not the truth.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Addison is a Searcher, she is able to see all the alternate paths when she has to make a decision. Basically, she's able to see, and live through, all the ways a certain choice will change her future and where that decison would lead. <br />This story is set in a modern day world, where a secret society of Paranormals with special mind abilities lives in a technologically advanced Compound, only rarely mixing with the Norms - the ordinary people not able to use any mind abilities. <br /> <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Doesn't help to waste my time thinking about would've-beens."<br />Laila whispers, "He says to the girl with a mind full of them.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />When Addison's parents tell her they are planning to divorce, she has to make a decision. Her father, whom she loves most, is leaving the Compound to live among the Norms, while her distanced mother is staing. Addison decides to Search in her mind both alternate paths. <br />Should she stay with her mother, friends, people with whom she's alike and with everyhing she has known, or leave her old life behind for the sake of being with the person she loves most and an unexplored future? Which path will Addison take? When a strange deaths of young teenagers strat to occure in the Para world, everything gets much more complicated. <br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Because an illusion is an illusion. Reality always exists despite the facade.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />This book is basically mix of contemporary and science fiction, which sounds maybe a bit contradictory but does actually works out here. It was very light on the sci-fi elements though.<br /><br /><i>Pivot Point</i>, while having many flaws, is such a page turner. The beggining is a bit generic, but after a while, the plot grippes you and makes sure you start questioning everything and whon't stop thinking about this book and all the possibe outcomes. I had also many problems with this book - the eye-roll-worthy tropes, my lack of deeper connection to the characters and their relationships, some generic parts of the story and Duke. Also, I think that the potential for this story was great and it could've been written and constructed in a better way.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I don't care when people think I'm an antisocial, controlling bookworm because that's what I am. It's when they interpret me wrong that I have a problem.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Pros:</u>
</b><br /><br />* The idea of this story<br /><br />* Unputdownable<br /><br />* The second half of this book improves tremendously<br /><br />* Great twists, not really shocking and some of them predictable, but revelations had an effect nonetheless<br /><br />* Trevor<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“When I read, I feel emotion all on my own. Emotion no living person is making me feel.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Cons:</u>
</b><br /><br />* Eye-roll-wothy tropes everywhere<br /><br />* Lots of generic filler in the story<br /><br />* Duke<br /><br />* Certain lack of depth of the characters<br /><br />* Way too much centerd on the two romances (not a love-triangle in this case though). Would've liked this story more if it was centered on other things as much as on the romances, as it was for the most part<br /><br />* Overall, I expected more from this <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“My bookcase is all yours.”<br />“I've just decided that those are my favorite five words in the world.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />----------------------------------------<br /><br /><u>After reading:</u><br /><br />Could not put this one down. This is the second Kasie West book in a row which I couldn't stop reading, honestly. I did expect a bit more from this - the idea of this story had tremendous potential. It was really tropey, but I also really liked the second part and some other things. RTC</span>
  <a data-text-id="3416367051254937740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1615591454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1615591454" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26439378-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491049557p2/26439378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1615591454?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/26439378-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615591454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13723749809659018161">This book had me hooked from the beginning and it was the ideal book to push me into reading more. Pivot Point was a light and easy book to read compared to many other paranormal/sci-fi books. It didn’t require a lot of thought and it was easy to get lost in the story. I didn’t exactly know what to expect because I’ve read all of Kasie West’s other books which were all contemporaries. I wouldn’t say this book is a big difference, it's similar to her other novels but with a twist. It was very dif</span>
  <span id="freeText13723749809659018161" style="display:none">This book had me hooked from the beginning and it was the ideal book to push me into reading more. Pivot Point was a light and easy book to read compared to many other paranormal/sci-fi books. It didn’t require a lot of thought and it was easy to get lost in the story. I didn’t exactly know what to expect because I’ve read all of Kasie West’s other books which were all contemporaries. I wouldn’t say this book is a big difference, it's similar to her other novels but with a twist. It was very difficult to stop reading and I definitely will be picking the second book straight after this review is written. <br /><br />Pivot Point follows Addison who lives in a place known as the Compound which is exterior to the ‘normal’ world. Inside the Compound the people each have various abilities which allow them to control specific things. Addie is a Searcher so when faced with a choice she is able to look in the future to see the alternate outcomes which are supposed to help her determine what to choose. Addie is confronted with the choice of which parent to live with after her parents announce they are having a divorce. She is to either live with her mother in the Compound or leave with her father to live with the Norms. Despite being able to see both paths Addie realises the decision will not be as easy as she thought. <br /><br />Kasie West has yet again managed to write an amazing novel that could not be put down. I loved getting to see the story progress through two different ways (That’s not the right way to put it but I don’t know how else to word it). Getting to see two alternative ways a person’s life could play out is something I have never read or watched before so it was something very different. I enjoyed the concept and it wasn’t annoying like I initially thought it would be. Surprisingly, there was no confusion between the two paths but that would probably be because it was easy to tell them apart. I also enjoyed seeing Addie’s experience through the two potential futures. The last hundred pages of this book did take a quite unexpected turn and it made this book so much better. <br /><br />The entire idea of the world Addie lived in was very interesting. I wouldn’t say unique but it was refreshing in a way. I loved the concept but I think it just needed to be executed in a better way. There need to be more world-building and a better explanation for why things were the way they were. There were a lot of plot holes in the book. I don’t know if this considered as a spoiler but I’m marking as one anyway. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I want to know how these people managed to unlock that part of their brain or be able to get such abilities. I also wanted to know how the compound was kept hidden. Was the government on it too because people have IDs in the normal world and the government knows everything. If this place was so top secret, why were they allowed to go into the normal world? The normal people even knew about their schools, I mean is that even a good idea. I think this might have been explained and I probably looked over it but how did the Compound football team play against other Norm teams. Would they stop playing the version where the ball flies and play it normally?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> These plot holes listed in the spoiler (there are probably more) just caused the book to lack something. They might be explained in the sequel but I doubt it. <br /><br />Addie was probably the best protagonist I’ve read about but that might be more because of personal reasons. I could relate to her soo much! First of all her love for books and words, in general, is something I’m sure most readers can relate to but it wasn’t just that. Addie is an anti-social person which is totally me but she also had this thing with silence when talking to someone. She doesn’t like it because it's awkward and she kind of starts panicking in a way and thinking (which is quoted from the book) “oh-crap-why-can’t-I-think-of-anything-to-say” which is exactly like me. It was also just her personality in general which I could relate to. Other than I found her so relatable she was still a character that was really likeable and I didn’t have any problems with her. <br /><br />Choosing between Duke and Trevor would be the easiest thing ever because I would definitely pick Trevor. Duke wasn’t a bad character at the beginning but when I met Trevor I started to like him more and then I didn’t care about Duke. I completely loved Duke at the beginning but then I didn’t. As the story progressed it was difficult to even like Duke and this whole popular jock guy thing just didn’t make it easier. Besides, Trevor was much better because he was just so perfect. I loved him so much more and I liked her life with him more. <br /><br />There were several unexpected things that occur towards the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I really didn’t expect Laila to die in one path or that Bobby was actually bad. I mean he did look shifty but still, it wasn’t until Addie went into his house where I started to piece some things together. I also didn’t expect that telekinesis wasn’t Duke’s ability and that he was a mood controller (crap I forgot the actual name). Although it does make sense when you look back at it. Addie always questioned her relationship with him when he wasn’t there but when he was it was like she was under spell (well she was in a way). Her choosing to stay was also something I didn’t expect. After Laila’s death in one path I really had no idea what she would do but before that, I thought she would have gone with her dad. Also, she erased Trevor after he asked her not to, how sad! I loved him so much and I didn’t want her to leave let alone forget about him.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The book ended sort of on a cliff-hanger and it felt kind of unfinished so I will definitely read the sequel as soon as possible. I’ve heard it picks off right where this one ends but I’m wondering right now, is it necessary? Maybe if this book was longer it could have been wrapped up? I’m not sure yet because I have yet to pick up the sequel so I’ll see after I read it. The only thing I’m not looking forward to is that I think it has Laila’s POV. I didn’t hate her but she just isn’t the character that I would to follow and see her perspective. She did do a lot of irritating things in this book. <br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed this book and I flew through it just like I always do with Kasie West’s books. Split Second is the last book I haven’t read by Kasie West and it is kind of sad because I love her books so much. She just manages to draw the reader right from the beginning and there’s no long intro to the story (although maybe this book needed one considering the total lack of world-building). Despite this novel having paranormal/sci-fi elements, there are a lot of contemporary aspects and a little bit of mystery in the mix so I would recommend this to a lot of people because it has something for everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13723749809659018161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elena Salvatore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44325911-elena-salvatore"><img alt="Elena Salvatore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553816124p2/44325911.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1947610459?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena Salvatore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena Salvatore" href="/user/show/44325911-elena-salvatore">Elena Salvatore</a>
      </span>

        rated it

  <i>Addison lives in a town where people have developed their human mind and are able to access a part of their brain which gives them "superpowers". <br/>For instance, her father is a human lie detector, her mother can convince you to do anything and her best friend can erase memories.<br/>Addie has the ability to see the future. Sort of....<br/>When she has to make a decision, she can see her life into the furture of every alternative, so that she can choose which path to take.<br/><br/>Wh</i></blockquote></span>

</blockquote><br><br><br>This is the first paranormal book that Kasie West has written and it is great.<br>I loved all her contemporary romance novells so I had no doubt that I will like this one too.<br><br>Of course the romance in this book played a huge part but the paranormal aspect was pleasantely surprising.<br><br><br>However the ending made me mad. Not because it was bad but because it was aggrivating.<br>Halfway through the book I knew what would happen and which reality she would choose, but the reasone she choose that reality was just plain stupid.<br><br>I do have alot of book pet peeves but the one thing that I hate most above all of them is that the protagonist chooses to keep some things hidden and thus complicating their lifes, even tho every desaster could've been avoided if they spoke up.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Addison choose the father that Bobby was behind all the deaths but because they didn't have any evidence other than her vision, they would keep a close eye on him and eventually found him guilty before he managed to kill all those other people.<br>But Addie didn't care about them because they weren't her bestfriends.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443865944ra/16423894.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then she could've told Laila the truth about Duke's powers and forbid her to tell anyone.<br>She could also tell her to keep away from Bobby because she saw something really dangerous about him.<br><br>And lastly she could've told Duke that she knows his secret and if he didn't play fair she would expose him.<br>Also he should tell Trey to fix Trevors back.<br><br>End, she would chose to live with her father and be happy with Trevor.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490301091ra/22300861.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But she didn't do any of those things because we need something for the second book and if she would do them, the story would have ended here.<br><i>(Not that I am mad about it)</i>, but here's to the publishers who wanted to have a series.<br><img <div id="review_462706213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462706213" />
    <a title="Emily Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13045626-emily-anne"><img alt="Emily Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533593667p2/13045626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462706213?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Anne" href="/user/show/13045626-emily-anne">Emily Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13045626-emily-anne?shelf=clever">clever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13045626-emily-anne?shelf=great-female-character">great-female-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13045626-emily-anne?shelf=great-male-character">great-male-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13045626-emily-anne?shelf=powers">powers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462706213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14002947176803086747">I don't know why, but I pre ordered this book 3 months before it came out, and I am so glad I did. Pivot Point glues you to it's pages, and I finished it in one night.<br/><br/>The book starts out very quickly. Addie comes home from her supernatural school to hear the news that her parents are getting a divorce. Her mom is staying in the Compound, while her dad is moving to the normal world. Addie has to pick who to live with.<br/><br/>She calls her best friend over and, to help decide, uses her powers as a searche</span>
  <span id="freeText14002947176803086747" style="display:none">I don't know why, but I pre ordered this book 3 months before it came out, and I am so glad I did. Pivot Point glues you to it's pages, and I finished it in one night.<br /><br />The book starts out very quickly. Addie comes home from her supernatural school to hear the news that her parents are getting a divorce. Her mom is staying in the Compound, while her dad is moving to the normal world. Addie has to pick who to live with.<br /><br />She calls her best friend over and, to help decide, uses her powers as a searcher to see both paths in the future. There is no dragging whatsoever in the beginning. You get a quick introduction, and then into the action. Just the way that keeps the audience interested in the book.<br /><br />One path, the one with her dad outside the compound, shows Addie adjusting to "normal" high school. She finds friends, one of which, Trevor, could be more of a friend. Addie learns valuable lessons about life outside her supernatural community. <br /><br />When with her mom, Addie hangs out with her best friend and a famous school football player, Duke. The paths intertwine, in each you'll earn unique information about a mystery. Another enjoyable aspect in the book. Each path also has it's consequences and perks. Very true to real life. <br /><br />Addie is a very relatable heroine. She is nice, realistic, and unique. I especially think book lovers will love and understand her. Her best friend, Laila, is a pretty cool character too. She is funny and supportive, although in some ways she is very alike other best friends in YA.<br /><br />The whole Compound idea is very interesting and fun to read about, each person has a power or ability. There are so many cool ideas the author throws into the book, human lie detectors, telekinetics, perceptives, mood controllers, and more. And the world created seems like a regular teens world, with the normal drama, only with a supernatural twist!<br /><br />Overall, I would recommend this to all supernatural lovers. The characters were deep and the plot and writing was addictive. Pivot Point is a great read!<br /><br />5/5 bookcases<br />I can't wait to read Kasie West's next novel, The Distance Between Us!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14002947176803086747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2129552-lauren-sugar-snark?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer485532834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17719566077316434810"><b>I had a sneaking suspicion that I might hate this book and when I found out it was set in a secret high school for teenagers with special abilities.</b> (Like the movie Sky High lol!) <b>I was thinking “Oh crap! Abort, abort!!”</b><br/><br/>I don’t think I have really enjoy a paranormal book set in high school since Vampire Academy and I must admit I was expecting this book to be something more along the lines of The Time Travellers Wife. But <b>this book is nothing like anything I have read before. WOW!</b><br/><br/>Addie lives in </span>
  <span id="freeText17719566077316434810" style="display:none"><b>I had a sneaking suspicion that I might hate this book and when I found out it was set in a secret high school for teenagers with special abilities.</b> (Like the movie Sky High lol!) <b>I was thinking “Oh crap! Abort, abort!!”</b><br><br>I don’t think I have really enjoy a paranormal book set in high school since Vampire Academy and I must admit I was expecting this book to be something more along the lines of The Time Travellers Wife. But <b>this book is nothing like anything I have read before. WOW!</b><br><br>Addie lives in a secret community (and goes to a secret high school) where everyone has special abilities. Her ability is to see the different outcomes/futures of the choices she makes. When her parents decide to get divorced Addie must make the choice of staying with her mom in the paranormal compound or going with her dad to live in the “normal” world. This leads Addie using her ability to see which choice is best...<br><br>The chapters of this book alternate from one potential path/reality to another and you might think that this would be confusing but <b>Holy Hell! it was well written!</b> In each version of Addie’s “reality” she has different friends, a different love interest and different issues that make her character grow and evolve. But the author also managed to interweave the two stories in a very clever and sometimes subtle way that I thought was quite brilliant.<br><br>There is a running mystery throughout this book and I really don’t want to go much further into plots or characters and their abilities because I feel like the smallest detail might be a spoiler and <b>I really do hope that you all read this book.</b><br><br>I started reading this book thinking I would read a few chapters and give up if it got too terrible, I wasn't even concentrating properly. (I was watching Batman Begins and read and the same time.)But the next thing I knew it was 3am my TV was on mute and I had devour this book! <b> My prejudice against YA Paranormals almost stopped me from reading this and that would have been really sad because it is one of the few really original books I have read in this genre for years!</b><br><br><b>Is this book perfect? </b>Not quite, but it is one hell of a debut!!<br><a href="http://www.freesmileys.org/smileys.php" title="Smiley" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363691i/715152.gif" alt="Smiley" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>P.S For those of you who don’t remember Sky High, this guy was the only memorable thing about it :)<br><a href="http://s1057.photobucket.com/user/poodding99/media/warren_zpse27d91eb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402047i/781186.jpg" alt=" photo warren_zpse27d91eb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_356467812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356467812" />
    <a title="Sara Raasch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5596336-sara-raasch"><img alt="Sara Raasch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450829490p2/5596336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356467812?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Raasch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Raasch" href="/user/show/5596336-sara-raasch">Sara Raasch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356467812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10517050309671517681">I'm going to lay out two possible futures for you. Are you ready?<br/><br/>So, you walk into a bookstore, and there on the shelf sits PIVOT POINT. In your pocket is your most recent wad of book-money, which you had intended to spend on your ever-growing collection of books about vampires. But then you see PP, a book that is completely vampire-free, and you think "Hm. Maybe today, I should try something different?"<br/><br/>These are the two futures, as laid out for you by me, the Knower of Futures:<br/><br/>1) If you buy PIV</span>
  <span id="freeText10517050309671517681" style="display:none">I'm going to lay out two possible futures for you. Are you ready?<br /><br />So, you walk into a bookstore, and there on the shelf sits PIVOT POINT. In your pocket is your most recent wad of book-money, which you had intended to spend on your ever-growing collection of books about vampires. But then you see PP, a book that is completely vampire-free, and you think "Hm. Maybe today, I should try something different?"<br /><br />These are the two futures, as laid out for you by me, the Knower of Futures:<br /><br />1) If you buy PIVOT POINT: You will at first think, "Oh wow, Kasie West is a cover model too??" and only later find out that no, she isn't actually, but DANG that girl is pretty close. You will whisk your new copy of PP home, cuddle up on a comfy chair/couch of your choice, and proceed to have the most mind-bending reading experience of your life. Alternating chapters told from alternating realities that align with frightening precision until you are left clutching the book and screaming out loud "WHAT THE FRENCH TOAST JUST HAPPENED????"<br /><br />2) If you buy yet another vampire book: You will not be able to leave the bookstore without an overwhelming feeling of regret and remorse and guilt, gnawing guilt, because SERIOUSLY, how many vampire books do you need, and you just wasted the opportunity to have your mind BLOWN TO PIECES. For shame, good sir. FOR SHAME.<br /><br />These are your futures, dear book-buyer. Read them, learn them, know them, because you will very soon be faced with this choice. And I hope, for your sake, that you enjoy having your mind severely blown. <br /><br />(Hint: PIVOT POINT is the right choice.) </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1859596357?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1859596357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4050009017870899267"><i>Pivot Point</i> was a pretty good and interesting book. However, the ending kind of confused me. It did also remind me of one of the endings from the Artemis Fowl series, I believe the third book, with the whole memory thing.<br/><br/>In this book you will meet Addison. She is a searcher and is able to see alternate paths when she has to make a decision. Sounds like that would come in handy with my life. One of the decisions she has to make is which parent to live with because her parents are getting a divorc</span>
  <span id="freeText4050009017870899267" style="display:none"><i>Pivot Point</i> was a pretty good and interesting book. However, the ending kind of confused me. It did also remind me of one of the endings from the Artemis Fowl series, I believe the third book, with the whole memory thing.<br /><br />In this book you will meet Addison. She is a searcher and is able to see alternate paths when she has to make a decision. Sounds like that would come in handy with my life. One of the decisions she has to make is which parent to live with because her parents are getting a divorce. It baffles me that she had to pick - she's a kid! When my parents got divorced I didn't get to choose which parent I wanted to live with. My sister and brother didn't either. Nope, all of the decision making went with my parents and the judge. Not us kids. <br /><br />The romance, aka sort of a love triangle but not really, was meh. At first I liked Duke but then he became a douche snozzle. Then there was Trevor, who I was kind of hesitant about liking in the first place but definitely sort of started to fall in love with his character. Besides these two, Addison is a quirky, smart, and strange main character. She just would say the oddest things like that hse hated someone without having a good reason as to why. Or saying someone is creepy just for the hell of it. The girl was strange yet likable in my eyes.<br /><br />Throughout the story you did get some twist and turns. Predictable twist and turns but still enjoyable. The only thing I would change about this book is the ending. It just confused me. Not like the Artemis Fowl book did because it made sense. He got his memory wiped - the end. However, with this ending it's like it happened to her yet she still choose what she wanted to do!?! I'm kind of baffled.. and feel like I might've missed something. I might have to reread it just to make sure.<br /><br />Overall, it was a likable book. I can totally see myself diving into the second one whenever I get my hands on it.</span>

          </span>
